Only metrics relevant or computable for this dataset are shown. If a metric is missing, not met, or not applicable, it is due to the dataset's characteristics or privacy analysis logicâ€”not a system limitation.

Metric explanations (include these in the summary):
- k-anonymity: Measures how well data can be disguised within a group. Low k-anonymity means individuals may be more easily re-identified.
- l-diversity: Ensures that within each group, there is a sufficient number of distinct values for sensitive attributes. Low l-diversity means sensitive values are too similar within groups.
- t-closeness: Measures how close the distribution of a sensitive attribute in a group is to the distribution in the overall dataset. High t-closeness indicates a higher risk of attribute disclosure.
- Re-identification risk: Estimates the probability that an individual can be re-identified from the dataset, given the quasi-identifiers and sensitive attributes. A higher value means a greater risk of re-identification.
Definitions for metric status (include these in the summary):
- Not met: The metric was evaluated, but the dataset did not satisfy the required threshold (e.g., k-anonymity threshold was set, but the data did not reach it).
- Not applicable: The metric does not apply to the dataset, often because of its structure, content, or the privacy configuration (e.g., t-closeness is only relevant for certain types of sensitive data).
- Omitted: The metric was not calculated at all, either because the Model Context Protocol tool determined it was unnecessary, the dataset lacked the required attributes, or the scan configuration did not request it.

You are a third-party privacy auditor. Given the following dataset and its privacy scan results, generate a clear, actionable, and human-readable summary for a non-technical audience. Include:
- The dataset name (no file paths): 2021Census_G01_NSW_LGA.csv

- Recommended actions (if any)

- An explicit risk level for this dataset (e.g., Low, Moderate, High), based on the findings
Only metrics relevant or computable for this dataset are shown. If a metric is missing, not met, or not applicable, it is due to the dataset's characteristics or privacy analysis logicâ€”not a system limitation.

Metric explanations (include these in the summary):
- k-anonymity: Measures how well data can be disguised within a group. Low k-anonymity means individuals may be more easily re-identified.
- l-diversity: Ensures that within each group, there is a sufficient number of distinct values for sensitive attributes. Low l-diversity means sensitive values are too similar within groups.
- t-closeness: Measures how close the distribution of a sensitive attribute in a group is to the distribution in the overall dataset. High t-closeness indicates a higher risk of attribute disclosure.
- Re-identification risk: Estimates the probability that an individual can be re-identified from the dataset, given the quasi-identifiers and sensitive attributes. A higher value means a greater risk of re-identification.
Definitions for metric status (include these in the summary):
- Not met: The metric was evaluated, but the dataset did not satisfy the required threshold (e.g., k-anonymity threshold was set, but the data did not reach it).
- Not applicable: The metric does not apply to the dataset, often because of its structure, content, or the privacy configuration (e.g., t-closeness is only relevant for certain types of sensitive data).
- Omitted: The metric was not calculated at all, either because the Model Context Protocol tool determined it was unnecessary, the dataset lacked the required attributes, or the scan configuration did not request it.

At the end, provide a short overall assessment and next steps for ongoing privacy protection.

Only metrics relevant or computable for this dataset are shown. If a metric is missing, not met, or not applicable, it is due to the dataset's characteristics or privacy analysis logicâ€”not a system limitation.

Metric explanations (include these in the summary):
- k-anonymity: Measures how well data can be disguised within a group. Low k-anonymity means individuals may be more easily re-identified.
- l-diversity: Ensures that within each group, there is a sufficient number of distinct values for sensitive attributes. Low l-diversity means sensitive values are too similar within groups.
- t-closeness: Measures how close the distribution of a sensitive attribute in a group is to the distribution in the overall dataset. High t-closeness indicates a higher risk of attribute disclosure.
- Re-identification risk: Estimates the probability that an individual can be re-identified from the dataset, given the quasi-identifiers and sensitive attributes. A higher value means a greater risk of re-identification.
Definitions for metric status (include these in the summary):
- Not met: The metric was evaluated, but the dataset did not satisfy the required threshold (e.g., k-anonymity threshold was set, but the data did not reach it).
- Not applicable: The metric does not apply to the dataset, often because of its structure, content, or the privacy configuration (e.g., t-closeness is only relevant for certain types of sensitive data).
- Omitted: The metric was not calculated at all, either because the Model Context Protocol tool determined it was unnecessary, the dataset lacked the required attributes, or the scan configuration did not request it.

- The dataset name (no file paths): 2021Census_G02_NSW_LGA.csv

Only metrics relevant or computable for this dataset are shown. If a metric is missing, not met, or not applicable, it is due to the dataset's characteristics or privacy analysis logicâ€”not a system limitation.

Metric explanations (include these in the summary):
- k-anonymity: Measures how well data can be disguised within a group. Low k-anonymity means individuals may be more easily re-identified.
- l-diversity: Ensures that within each group, there is a sufficient number of distinct values for sensitive attributes. Low l-diversity means sensitive values are too similar within groups.
- t-closeness: Measures how close the distribution of a sensitive attribute in a group is to the distribution in the overall dataset. High t-closeness indicates a higher risk of attribute disclosure.
- Re-identification risk: Estimates the probability that an individual can be re-identified from the dataset, given the quasi-identifiers and sensitive attributes. A higher value means a greater risk of re-identification.
Definitions for metric status (include these in the summary):
- Not met: The metric was evaluated, but the dataset did not satisfy the required threshold (e.g., k-anonymity threshold was set, but the data did not reach it).
- Not applicable: The metric does not apply to the dataset, often because of its structure, content, or the privacy configuration (e.g., t-closeness is only relevant for certain types of sensitive data).
- Omitted: The metric was not calculated at all, either because the Model Context Protocol tool determined it was unnecessary, the dataset lacked the required attributes, or the scan configuration did not request it.

At the end, provide a short overall assessment and next steps for ongoing privacy protection.

Only metrics relevant or computable for this dataset are shown. If a metric is missing, not met, or not applicable, it is due to the dataset's characteristics or privacy analysis logicâ€”not a system limitation.

Metric explanations (include these in the summary):
- k-anonymity: Measures how well data can be disguised within a group. Low k-anonymity means individuals may be more easily re-identified.
- l-diversity: Ensures that within each group, there is a sufficient number of distinct values for sensitive attributes. Low l-diversity means sensitive values are too similar within groups.
- t-closeness: Measures how close the distribution of a sensitive attribute in a group is to the distribution in the overall dataset. High t-closeness indicates a higher risk of attribute disclosure.
- Re-identification risk: Estimates the probability that an individual can be re-identified from the dataset, given the quasi-identifiers and sensitive attributes. A higher value means a greater risk of re-identification.
Definitions for metric status (include these in the summary):
- Not met: The metric was evaluated, but the dataset did not satisfy the required threshold (e.g., k-anonymity threshold was set, but the data did not reach it).
- Not applicable: The metric does not apply to the dataset, often because of its structure, content, or the privacy configuration (e.g., t-closeness is only relevant for certain types of sensitive data).
- Omitted: The metric was not calculated at all, either because the Model Context Protocol tool determined it was unnecessary, the dataset lacked the required attributes, or the scan configuration did not request it.

At the end, provide a short overall assessment and next steps for ongoing privacy protection.

[SummariserAgent] Prompt to LLM: System: Data Privacy Impact Assessment & Reporting
You are a third-party privacy auditor. Given the following dataset and its privacy scan results, generate a clear, actionable, and human-readable summary for a non-technical audience. Include:
- The dataset name (no file paths): 2021Census_G03_NSW_LGA.csv
- Any privacy risks or flags, with a brief explanation
- Recommended actions (if any)
- Model Context Protocol findings: k-anonymity, l-diversity, t-closeness, re-identification risk, and the threshold values used
- An explicit risk level for this dataset (e.g., Low, Moderate, High), based on the findings
Only metrics relevant or computable for this dataset are shown. If a metric is missing, not met, or not applicable, it is due to the dataset's characteristics or privacy analysis logicâ€”not a system limitation.

Metric explanations (include these in the summary):
- k-anonymity: Measures how well data can be disguised within a group. Low k-anonymity means individuals may be more easily re-identified.
- l-diversity: Ensures that within each group, there is a sufficient number of distinct values for sensitive attributes. Low l-diversity means sensitive values are too similar within groups.
- t-closeness: Measures how close the distribution of a sensitive attribute in a group is to the distribution in the overall dataset. High t-closeness indicates a higher risk of attribute disclosure.
- Re-identification risk: Estimates the probability that an individual can be re-identified from the dataset, given the quasi-identifiers and sensitive attributes. A higher value means a greater risk of re-identification.
Definitions for metric status (include these in the summary):
- Not met: The metric was evaluated, but the dataset did not satisfy the required threshold (e.g., k-anonymity threshold was set, but the data did not reach it).
- Not applicable: The metric does not apply to the dataset, often because of its structure, content, or the privacy configuration (e.g., t-closeness is only relevant for certain types of sensitive data).
- Omitted: The metric was not calculated at all, either because the Model Context Protocol tool determined it was unnecessary, the dataset lacked the required attributes, or the scan configuration did not request it.

At the end, provide a short overall assessment and next steps for ongoing privacy protection.

You are a third-party privacy auditor. Given the following dataset and its privacy scan results, generate a clear, actionable, and human-readable summary for a non-technical audience. Include:
- The dataset name (no file paths): /Users/gracebilliris/Projects/dpiar-agentic-privacy-monitor/agentic-privacy-monitor/backend/test-files/synthetic_privacy_test.csv
- Any privacy risks or flags, with a brief explanation
- Recommended actions (if any)
- Model Context Protocol findings: k-anonymity, l-diversity, t-closeness, re-identification risk, and the threshold values used
- An explicit risk level for this dataset (e.g., Low, Moderate, High), based on the findings
Only metrics relevant or computable for this dataset are shown. If a metric is missing, not met, or not applicable, it is due to the dataset's characteristics or privacy analysis logicâ€”not a system limitation.

Metric explanations (include these in the summary):
- k-anonymity: Measures how well data can be disguised within a group. Low k-anonymity means individuals may be more easily re-identified.
- l-diversity: Ensures that within each group, there is a sufficient number of distinct values for sensitive attributes. Low l-diversity means sensitive values are too similar within groups.
- t-closeness: Measures how close the distribution of a sensitive attribute in a group is to the distribution in the overall dataset. High t-closeness indicates a higher risk of attribute disclosure.
- Re-identification risk: Estimates the probability that an individual can be re-identified from the dataset, given the quasi-identifiers and sensitive attributes. A higher value means a greater risk of re-identification.
Definitions for metric status (include these in the summary):
- Not met: The metric was evaluated, but the dataset did not satisfy the required threshold (e.g., k-anonymity threshold was set, but the data did not reach it).
- Not applicable: The metric does not apply to the dataset, often because of its structure, content, or the privacy configuration (e.g., t-closeness is only relevant for certain types of sensitive data).
- Omitted: The metric was not calculated at all, either because the Model Context Protocol tool determined it was unnecessary, the dataset lacked the required attributes, or the scan configuration did not request it.

At the end, provide a short overall assessment and next steps for ongoing privacy protection.

Only metrics relevant or computable for this dataset are shown. If a metric is missing, not met, or not applicable, it is due to the dataset's characteristics or privacy analysis logicâ€”not a system limitation.

Metric explanations (include these in the summary):
- k-anonymity: Measures how well data can be disguised within a group. Low k-anonymity means individuals may be more easily re-identified.
- l-diversity: Ensures that within each group, there is a sufficient number of distinct values for sensitive attributes. Low l-diversity means sensitive values are too similar within groups.
- t-closeness: Measures how close the distribution of a sensitive attribute in a group is to the distribution in the overall dataset. High t-closeness indicates a higher risk of attribute disclosure.
- Re-identification risk: Estimates the probability that an individual can be re-identified from the dataset, given the quasi-identifiers and sensitive attributes. A higher value means a greater risk of re-identification.
Definitions for metric status (include these in the summary):
- Not met: The metric was evaluated, but the dataset did not satisfy the required threshold (e.g., k-anonymity threshold was set, but the data did not reach it).
- Not applicable: The metric does not apply to the dataset, often because of its structure, content, or the privacy configuration (e.g., t-closeness is only relevant for certain types of sensitive data).
- Omitted: The metric was not calculated at all, either because the Model Context Protocol tool determined it was unnecessary, the dataset lacked the required attributes, or the scan configuration did not request it.

At the end, provide a short overall assessment and next steps for ongoing privacy protection.

Only metrics relevant or computable for this dataset are shown. If a metric is missing, not met, or not applicable, it is due to the dataset's characteristics or privacy analysis logicâ€”not a system limitation.

Metric explanations (include these in the summary):
- k-anonymity: Measures how well data can be disguised within a group. Low k-anonymity means individuals may be more easily re-identified.
- l-diversity: Ensures that within each group, there is a sufficient number of distinct values for sensitive attributes. Low l-diversity means sensitive values are too similar within groups.
- t-closeness: Measures how close the distribution of a sensitive attribute in a group is to the distribution in the overall dataset. High t-closeness indicates a higher risk of attribute disclosure.
- Re-identification risk: Estimates the probability that an individual can be re-identified from the dataset, given the quasi-identifiers and sensitive attributes. A higher value means a greater risk of re-identification.
Definitions for metric status (include these in the summary):
- Not met: The metric was evaluated, but the dataset did not satisfy the required threshold (e.g., k-anonymity threshold was set, but the data did not reach it).
- Not applicable: The metric does not apply to the dataset, often because of its structure, content, or the privacy configuration (e.g., t-closeness is only relevant for certain types of sensitive data).
- Omitted: The metric was not calculated at all, either because the Model Context Protocol tool determined it was unnecessary, the dataset lacked the required attributes, or the scan configuration did not request it.

At the end, provide a short overall assessment and next steps for ongoing privacy protection.

[SummariserAgent] Prompt to LLM: System: Data Privacy Impact Assessment & Reporting
You are a third-party privacy auditor. Given the following dataset and its privacy scan results, generate a clear, actionable, and human-readable summary for a non-technical audience. Include:
- The dataset name (no file paths): types-of-health-insurance-coverage-by-age.csv
- Any privacy risks or flags, with a brief explanation
- Recommended actions (if any)
- Model Context Protocol findings: k-anonymity, l-diversity, t-closeness, re-identification risk, and the threshold values used
- An explicit risk level for this dataset (e.g., Low, Moderate, High), based on the findings
Only metrics relevant or computable for this dataset are shown. If a metric is missing, not met, or not applicable, it is due to the dataset's characteristics or privacy analysis logicâ€”not a system limitation.

Metric explanations (include these in the summary):
- k-anonymity: Measures how well data can be disguised within a group. Low k-anonymity means individuals may be more easily re-identified.
- l-diversity: Ensures that within each group, there is a sufficient number of distinct values for sensitive attributes. Low l-diversity means sensitive values are too similar within groups.
- t-closeness: Measures how close the distribution of a sensitive attribute in a group is to the distribution in the overall dataset. High t-closeness indicates a higher risk of attribute disclosure.
- Re-identification risk: Estimates the probability that an individual can be re-identified from the dataset, given the quasi-identifiers and sensitive attributes. A higher value means a greater risk of re-identification.
Definitions for metric status (include these in the summary):
- Not met: The metric was evaluated, but the dataset did not satisfy the required threshold (e.g., k-anonymity threshold was set, but the data did not reach it).
- Not applicable: The metric does not apply to the dataset, often because of its structure, content, or the privacy configuration (e.g., t-closeness is only relevant for certain types of sensitive data).
- Omitted: The metric was not calculated at all, either because the Model Context Protocol tool determined it was unnecessary, the dataset lacked the required attributes, or the scan configuration did not request it.

At the end, provide a short overall assessment and next steps for ongoing privacy protection.

System: Data Privacy Impact Assessment & Reporting
You are a third-party privacy auditor. Given the following datasets and their privacy scan results, generate a clear, actionable, and human-readable summary for a non-technical audience. For each dataset, include:
- The dataset name (no file paths)
- Any privacy risks or flags, with a brief explanation
- Recommended actions (if any)
- Model Context Protocol findings: k-anonymity, l-diversity, t-closeness, re-identification risk, and the threshold values used. IMPORTANT: Always report the actual metric values (even if low, zero, or below threshold). Do NOT say 'not calculated', 'not applicable', or 'not evaluated' unless the value is truly missing. If a metric is below threshold, state the value and that it did not meet the threshold.
- An explicit risk level for each dataset (e.g., Low, Moderate, High), based on the findings
For each dataset, include a section titled 'MCP Metric Findings' and present the following as a bullet list or table:
  - k-anonymity: minimum, average, required threshold, and status (Met/Not met/Not applicable)
  - l-diversity: minimum, average, method, required threshold, and status
  - t-closeness: maximum, average, method, required threshold, and status
  - re-identification risk: value, required threshold, and status
Always include the actual values and thresholds for each metric, even if the metric is not met.

Metric explanations (include these in the summary):
- k-anonymity: Measures how well data can be disguised within a group. Low k-anonymity means individuals may be more easily re-identified.
- l-diversity: Ensures that within each group, there is a sufficient number of distinct values for sensitive attributes. Low l-diversity means sensitive values are too similar within groups.
- t-closeness: Measures how close the distribution of a sensitive attribute in a group is to the distribution in the overall dataset. High t-closeness indicates a higher risk of attribute disclosure.
- Re-identification risk: Estimates the probability that an individual can be re-identified from the dataset, given the quasi-identifiers and sensitive attributes. A higher value means a greater risk of re-identification.
Definitions for metric status (include these in the summary):
- Not met: The metric was evaluated, but the dataset did not satisfy the required threshold (e.g., k-anonymity threshold was set, but the data did not reach it).
- Not applicable: The metric does not apply to the dataset, often because of its structure, content, or the privacy configuration (e.g., t-closeness is only relevant for certain types of sensitive data).
- Omitted: The metric was not calculated at all, either because the Model Context Protocol tool determined it was unnecessary, the dataset lacked the required attributes, or the scan configuration did not request it.

At the end, provide a short overall assessment and next steps for ongoing privacy protection. Also, provide an explicit overall risk level (e.g., Low, Moderate, High) for all datasets combined, based on your findings.
